          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8838148-tatiana-and-alexander">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739445050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3190356097148237084"><br/><b>
  <i>*** 5++++ INFINITE, HEARTBREAKING, UNFORGETTABLE AND ALL CONSUMING STARS *** </i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/10/irzu.jpg/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381794814i/5308999.jpg' alt='Image Hosted by ImageShack.us' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I just can't get over how much IN LOVE I am with these books...with this EPIC and TIMELESS story...with Tatiana and Alexander...<br/>It truly is the most consuming and beautiful love story I ever read! Full of devotion, ache, longing, angst, despair and above all hope. If they were lucky to find each other, they will always find away towards each other. They can't conceive a world without the other in it!<br/><br/>So there are</span>
  <span id="freeText3190356097148237084" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>*** 5++++ INFINITE, HEARTBREAKING, UNFORGETTABLE AND ALL CONSUMING STARS *** </i>
</b><br><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/10/irzu.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381794814i/5308999.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I just can't get over how much IN LOVE I am with these books...with this EPIC and TIMELESS story...with Tatiana and Alexander...<br>It truly is the most consuming and beautiful love story I ever read! Full of devotion, ache, longing, angst, despair and above all hope. If they were lucky to find each other, they will always find away towards each other. They can't conceive a world without the other in it!<br><br>So there are love stories and then there are Tatia and Shura story...<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/443/9xcw.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381591474i/5074275._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After being torn apart,Tania and Shura are trying to survive in a world consumed by war, trying to survive without each other.<br><br>The book goes back and forth with both POV's...showing her journey to her new life in NY, with their son Anthony.<br> And showing how Alex tale of survival, from the NKVD interrogations, to the penal battalion to POW camps. We also get several "flashbacks" of Shura's life before the war, since he was a little kid leaving America for Soviet Union to many key moments of his life, that molded him to the man we first met in the previous book!<br><br><u>Tatiana </u><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/547/z68a.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381794814i/5309000.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She is most definitely one of my favorite heroines EVER! The most selfless, brave and resilient character! <br>She never gives up and she will do everything for the love of her life!<br><br>How can she go on, if she left her soul behind?<br><br><b>
  <i>“Live as if you have faith,” she said, “and faith shall be<br>given to you.” </i>
</b><br><br><u>Alexander </u><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/826/6k1r.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381794814i/5309001.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>*sigh<br><br>Shura, Shura, my precious Shura &lt;3 <br>Could I love him more? I don't think so! What he went through in this book just broke my heart...constantly holding on in his memories of her,of his everything. At all costs he must survive and get back to her. No matter how impossible it seems, he will never give up.<br><br>The flashbacks gave a whole new take on his actions and all he went through. Even as a teen he truly was the wise one, and could see what his parents denied to see.<br>And then,we see how one moment changed the course of his life forever.<br><br>In the whole book, many of his chapters were the most heartbreaking I ever read and left me a sobbing mess...from the bittersweet memories of Lazarevo, where he felt everything he hoped for slipped through his fingers, to the last time he saw his father, or the "delusions" he had with Tatia and with his father...<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/824/x0os.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381848697ra/5349311.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>
  <i>"Don't worry, Dad. I'll make you proud. I'll be ungreedy and unselfish, unprideful and unvengeful. I'll be as hard a man as they come. Let's go. I'm ready."<br>"I don't want you to be a hard man, Alexander. I want you to be a good man."Harold paused. "A better man than me." </i>
</b><br><br>You are Shura, you sure are!<br><br><u>Overall </u><br><br>I'm starting to lack words to describe how I think this series is PERFECTION! <br>It'll stay with my forever and ever!<br><br>Now, did you get how much I love this book? ;)<br><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/209/uma.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381848697ra/5349312.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/14/ow1z.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2307332097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2307332097" />
    <a title="Sharon Metcalf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49089020-sharon-metcalf"><img alt="Sharon Metcalf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451815807p2/49089020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2307332097?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Metcalf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Metcalf" href="/user/show/49089020-sharon-metcalf">Sharon Metcalf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007175765" href="/book/show/2974930-the-bridge-to-holy-cross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49089020-sharon-metcalf?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2307332097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9871224806582243399">The Bronze Horseman was a beautiful love story set in war torn Russia.    Paulina Simons ended book one on a note of young love rudely interrupted by war,  their lives ripped apart.    This almost guaranteed readers would be desperate to see Tatiana and Alexander reuinited.  I know I was.    The second instalment of the trilogy, Tatiana and Alexander (or The Bridge To Holy Cross as it's also known) was that story.<br/><br/>Tatiana had escaped to America where their son Anthony was born.   Meanwhile  Alexa</span>
  <span id="freeText9871224806582243399" style="display:none">The Bronze Horseman was a beautiful love story set in war torn Russia.    Paulina Simons ended book one on a note of young love rudely interrupted by war,  their lives ripped apart.    This almost guaranteed readers would be desperate to see Tatiana and Alexander reuinited.  I know I was.    The second instalment of the trilogy, Tatiana and Alexander (or The Bridge To Holy Cross as it's also known) was that story.<br /><br />Tatiana had escaped to America where their son Anthony was born.   Meanwhile  Alexander was in Russsia enduring the very worst conditions imaginable.     Whereas Tatiana is busy filling her days as a nurse at Ellis Island, helping other refugees and raising their son, Alexander is being treated as a criminal, he's sent to the frontline where lives are disposible, where he's injured and  starved.      Each of their stories overflowed with grief.    For both Alexander and Tatiana there was plenty of reminiscing of their times together but as the years progressed, instead of getting easier their grief became insurmountable, their desperation unbearable.   When Tatiana eventually finds the evidence she needs that Alexander may still be alive she takes matters into her own hands and returns to Russia hellbent upon rescuing her man.<br /><br />From the ouset all I wanted was to see them reunited but theirs was no easy path.  Having come this far with Tatiana and Alexander through their struggles I'm eager to get started on The Summer Garden.   As I read book two I couldn't help pondering how the worlds population righted itself after the tragedies and traumas of WWII.    How did individuals, families, communities move on and not get bogged down in despair, in depression, in PTSD?    There must have been literally millions of people who simply could not move on with their lives and losses post-war.  Only time (and the 742 pages) will tell what  Paulina Simons has in store for Tatiana and Alexander in their post-war lives but my  hope is for them to finally find happiness, together - away from Russia - in America,  with their son Anthony.    Whatever the case, I'm sure it will not disappoint and I trust her implicitly to take them and me where we need to go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9871224806582243399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4312560371853317221" style="display:none">Finishing this book leaves me almost breathless. Throughout all of its 560 pages, I was kept captivated. My heart was in my throat and my feelings were on edge. Paullina Simons' love story between Tatiana and Alexander, combined with their fatal lives during World War II, drags me in and leaves me completely anxious inside. <br />Even though the storyline in this book is quite different from the first book, I loved it so much! I needed to know what would happen to our two main characters and I cared deeply for them. Yes, I still have a problem with the way Alexander sometimes behaves but that's a slight error in a big and beautiful masterpiece. I can only say: Read this story! You will not regret it :) </span>

<div id="review_507561155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/507561155" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/507561155?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8838148-tatiana-and-alexander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden?shelf=favorite-historical-romance">favorite-historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507561155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer561178429903751746">The first half of this book had me worried since quite a bit of it was nothing more than flashbacks to the first book. But the flashbacks eventually faded away, and I was left to finish the rest of the tale, which was also a bit draining because I kept wondering <i>when</i> Alexander and Tatiana were <i>finally</i> going to see each other again. This book, like its predecessor, is a bit melodramatic, but Paullina Simons is a master manipulator; normally melodrama makes me roll my eyes or snicker, but this mel</span>
  <span id="freeText561178429903751746" style="display:none">The first half of this book had me worried since quite a bit of it was nothing more than flashbacks to the first book. But the flashbacks eventually faded away, and I was left to finish the rest of the tale, which was also a bit draining because I kept wondering <i>when</i> Alexander and Tatiana were <i>finally</i> going to see each other again. This book, like its predecessor, is a bit melodramatic, but Paullina Simons is a master manipulator; normally melodrama makes me roll my eyes or snicker, but this melodrama left me with that vaguely pressurized feeling in my chest like I was going to cry at any minute. Even during action scenes! I just wanted there to be something <i>happy</i> so badly that whenever something else went wrong, I wanted to start bawling and screaming about the unfairness of it all. <br /><br />So yeah, I guess you could say Paullina Simons knows how to bring out my inner (emotionally unstable) drama queen. <br /><br />It was a fun ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="561178429903751746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3181679329077951734">The bronze horseman was perfect, absolutely perfect. This just felt too forced, and also like I was re-reading too much of the original story, unfortunately it dulled the magic of that first book. I will read book three, I can't end Tatiana and Alexander's story like this.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_572159036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572159036" />
    <a title="M. ~ B&amp;B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14479657-m-b-b"><img alt="M. ~ B&amp;B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435261660p2/14479657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/572159036?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M. ~ B&amp;B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M. ~ B&amp;B" href="/user/show/14479657-m-b-b">M. ~ B&amp;B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062020253" href="/book/show/8467722-tatiana-and-alexander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=cried-my-heart-out">cried-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=inspiring-and-beautiful">inspiring-and-beautiful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=emotionally-draining">emotionally-draining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=heartbreakingly-beautiful">heartbreakingly-beautiful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14479657-m-b-b?shelf=infinite-amount-of-stars">infinite-amount-of-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer572159036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7221641934871585168"><b><i>Though much is taken, much abides; and though we are not now that strength which in old days moved earth and heaven, that which we are, we are—<br/></i><br/>Unyielding</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>***This review contains spoilers for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10849572.The_Bronze_Horseman__Tatiana_and_Alexander___1_' title='The Bronze Horseman (Tatiana and Alexander, #1) by Paullina Simons' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bronze Horseman</a>. Under no circumstances read this review if you haven't read the first book in the trilogy yet.***<br/><br/><br/><br/>Once again, Paullina Simons has rendered me speechless. This book has been emotional torture from beginning to end. I loved every page and every word I read. It was just pure perfection. I got</span>
  <span id="freeText7221641934871585168" style="display:none"><b><i>Though much is taken, much abides; and though we are not now that strength which in old days moved earth and heaven, that which we are, we are—<br></i><br>Unyielding</b><br><br><br><br>***This review contains spoilers for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10849572.The_Bronze_Horseman__Tatiana_and_Alexander___1_" title="The Bronze Horseman (Tatiana and Alexander, #1) by Paullina Simons" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bronze Horseman</a>. Under no circumstances read this review if you haven't read the first book in the trilogy yet.***<br><br><br><br>Once again, Paullina Simons has rendered me speechless. This book has been emotional torture from beginning to end. I loved every page and every word I read. It was just pure perfection. I got very emotional from the beginning and the emotions kept building up. I'd spill a few tears every now and then, but at one point I started full on sobbing and just sobbed my way through the rest of the book. This book was extremely touching, moving and just beautiful. This was the ultimate story about <i>love</i> and <i>loss</i>.<br><br>A love that started on the first day of war could never be peaceful. And so it wasn't. All it took was one glance, one look, and their lives would never be the same again. <br><br><b>
  <i>She was in a world Alexander had never seen, swimming on the moon in a sea of tranquility. [...] On that sunlit Sunday, Alexander knew nothing, thought nothing, imagined nothing. He forgot Dimitri and war and the Soviet Union and escape plans, and even America, and crossed the street for Tatiana Metanova.</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>He had found her, a Lazarevo orphan waiting for him, and made her whole.</i>
</b><br><br>Tatiana and Alexander have an extraordinary love that goes deeper than any other love I've read about. It is so touching, so real and so pure, that the loss of that love is unimaginable. Both Tatiana and Alexander were willing to risk their own life to save the other, but at the same time neither one of them was willing to go on without the other.<br><br><b>
  <i>I will go to the wall as your wife and never regret a second I spent with you.</i>
</b><br><br>When betrayal and deceit throw Alexander in the claws of the NKVD, he makes sure that his wife and their baby are safe. Tania, who now has to consider her baby's life too, makes her way to New York thinking her husband's dead.<br><br><b>
  <i>Where did they teach you how to live after you'd lost it all? [...] How was she going to get through losing him without him?</i>
</b><br><br>Alexander and Tatiana were literally each other's halves. One complementing the other and without each other they're lost. <br><br><b>
  <i>In Alexander’s life there was one thread that could not be broken by death, by distance, by time, by war. Could not be broken. As long as I am in the world, she said with her breath and her body, as long as I am, you are permanent, soldier.</i>
</b><br><br>Alexander didn't get executed, but was sent to command a penal battalion. While fighting to keep his life, she was all he could think about. She was the only thing that kept him alive and kept him going in Soviet Russia. He <i>loves her as much as it is possible for a man to love a woman.</i> His only goal was to get back to her again, so he could be whole again. <br><br><b>
  <i>Have you been looking for me? she had once asked him, and he replied, All my life.</i>
</b><br><br>As she had been looking for him. In New York the only face she kept seeing everywhere was his. The only face she kept looking for was his. The only hand she wanted to hold was his and the only lips she wanted to kiss were his. Tatiana was alive, but she wasn't living.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415014i/818912.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Today with every breath of the past she colored her breath of the future, with every blink of her eye, Alexander bore himself deeper and deeper inside her until the whole of what they were together blinded her from seeing what else might be in the world for her.<br><br>[...]<br><br>As she nursed her boy, Tatiana’s salty tears fell on his face that she didn’t bother to wipe, and in her tears and in her milk and in her heart only one word struck the clock of her soul on the stroke of every minute: Alexander.</i>
</b><br><br>My heart broke together with theirs. Her being away from him, him being away from her.. It was too much. Yet I loved the torture and the emotions it got out of me. It had gotten to the point where the single mention of Lazarevo reduced me to tears. And all my friends know I don't usually cry over books.<br><br><b>
  <i>Will you remember that? Anywhere you are, if you can look up and find Perseus in the sky, find that smile, and hear the galactic wind whisper your name, you’ll know it’s me, calling for you…calling you back to Lazarevo.</i>
</b><br><br>Even though she "knew" he was dead, she couldn't help but shake the feeling that maybe he wasn't. That maybe he needed her. That maybe she should go find him.<br><br><b><i>In the ocean, her arm outstretched to God, was Lady Liberty and on the fire escape was Tatiana, sitting in the three-in-the-morning air, listening across the ocean for the breathing of one man.</i> The king among men.</b><br><br>Tatiana's character kept amazing me over and over again. I cannot express how much I love her and how awesome I think she is. <br><br><b>
  <i>She was as resolute as ever, as fully loving, as completely giving, intensely tender, unbearably moving, as always affecting him utterly.</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Tania is at her core a happy soul, a resilient person. She is loyal and she is true, she is unyielding and relentless, but she also feels a child’s delight for the smallest things.</i>
</b><br><br>Her kindness was often mistaken for weakness, but she was everything but weak. Tatiana is the strongest female character I've ever read about. She's also the smartest and the most loyal one.<br><br><b>
  <i>"What if he is wondering why it’s taking me so long to come and find him, and I don’t come? Why don’t I come?”<br>“Why would he be waiting?”<br>“Because he knows what I am. I won’t leave him."</i>
</b><br><br>Alexander possessed the same strength and loyalty. Even when there seemed to be no way out, he never lost hope. He never gave up on finding his way back to her, because she was his only <i>life force</i> and the <i>brightest star in the sky</i>.<br><br><b>
  <i>"This is it, isn’t it? There is no way out.”<br>“You don’t think there is, but there is. We just haven’t thought of it."</i>
</b><br><br>This book gave us a lot of insight on what Alexander was like as a kid and how he became the man he is now. It tells us the story of Harold and Jane Barrington and how they saw their Soviet dream fall into pieces and how Alexander survived from it up till the moment where he meets Tania. The book switches back and forth between three different stories (Alexander's past, his present and Tania's present) and about halfway it becomes two stories/POV (Alexander's present and Tania's present). I loved this variation in stories. It kept it interesting and enjoyable to read.<br><br>I loved how there were many flashbacks and memories of book one of the trilogy. You could really see how symbolic everything was and how well it all connected with each other.<br><br><b>
  <i>I am going to lie down on his sled and close my eyes and he will pull me along the snow to my Fifth Soviet building, except when we get there, I will not feel his hand on my cheek.'<br><br>[...]<br><br>Courage, babe. Get up, get up for me, and go on. Go on, go take care of our son, and I will take care of you.</i>
</b><br><br>It's funny how everything in book one was so different from the way things were in book two. It's funny how life changed drastically for the both of them. <i>Dive into hope, or die in despair</i>. They dived into hope and it got them through the toughest times of their lives. I cannot wait to continue the journey in book three and see what more life has in store for them. My Tatiana &amp; Alexander, I will never forget them.<br><br><b>
  <i>We walk alone through this world, but if we’re lucky, we have a moment of belonging to something, to someone, that sustains us through a lifetime of loneliness.<br><br>For an evening minute I touched him again and grew red wings and was young again in the Summer Garden, and had hope and eternal life.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7221641934871585168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31348515-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458306439p2/31348515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476613269?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/31348515-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061987465" href="/book/show/7180853-tatiana-and-alexander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31348515-vivian?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476613269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16175406494073685140">"Will you remember that? Anywhere you are, if you can look up and find Perseus in the sky, find that smile, and hear the galactic wind whisper your name, you'll know that it's me, calling for you... calling you back to Lazarevo. (Alexander)” <br/><br/>I can't express my love enough for this series. I absolutely loved this book. Tatiana and Alexander teaches us what real love is really about. A love that war, hardship, loneliness, time and distance can't break, can't free them. <br/><br/>I have to say I really enjoy</span>
  <span id="freeText16175406494073685140" style="display:none">"Will you remember that? Anywhere you are, if you can look up and find Perseus in the sky, find that smile, and hear the galactic wind whisper your name, you'll know that it's me, calling for you... calling you back to Lazarevo. (Alexander)” <br /><br />I can't express my love enough for this series. I absolutely loved this book. Tatiana and Alexander teaches us what real love is really about. A love that war, hardship, loneliness, time and distance can't break, can't free them. <br /><br />I have to say I really enjoyed this book a lot. You get to learn a lot more about Alexander's past and how he became the man he was from his point of view. From childhood life in America before coming to the Soviet Union to the day he met Tatiana and even the time their spend apart after they've met. I felt more connected to him and to his life, to Tatiana and to his mother, who was a big part of him sill. (MORE ABOUT ALEXANDER IN MY BLOG)<br /><br />I admire Tatiana's heart and strength in New York with her son and new life. That despite a comfortable life and new friends she kept Alexander's memory alive inside of her, and by being kind and generous with others, for some reason the gods kept him alive for her too. (MORE ABOUT TATIANA IN MY BLOG)<br /><br />The reunion between Tatiana and Alexander was beautiful, and very emotional to me. I was beginning to think they weren't going to make it. As usual Tatiana wouldn't take no for an answer and did all in her power to get Alexander to come to America with her. She can't take the bronze horseman's pursuing her any longer. <br /><br />But at the end, after all the struggles, all the suffering all the war. Alexander is changed a little, and Tatiana too. Will their love be strong enough to adapt to their years apart? Their doubts and fears? Their weakness and their quiet? <br /><br />I sense a lot of heart troubles ahead for them...<br /><br />TO READ THE COMPLETE REVIEW, PLEASE VISITE MY BLOG!<br /><br />THANK YOU!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16175406494073685140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/915907074?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne OK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne OK" href="/user/show/285610-anne-ok">Anne OK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8838148-tatiana-and-alexander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/285610-anne-ok?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer915907074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1022702056107299927">While reading this highly emotional sequel, I found myself humming Neil Diamond’s “Coming to America” song with tears streaming down my cheeks. <br/><br/>Even better than the first installment and much easier to fall into. The lovers are torn apart. Tatiana is in America ripped with grief. And Alexander’s situation finds him facing execution for treason and espionage. The character development has blossomed. And the details and writing remain unapproachable. The author has a magical touch with all the his</span>
  <span id="freeText1022702056107299927" style="display:none">While reading this highly emotional sequel, I found myself humming Neil Diamond’s “Coming to America” song with tears streaming down my cheeks. <br /><br />Even better than the first installment and much easier to fall into. The lovers are torn apart. Tatiana is in America ripped with grief. And Alexander’s situation finds him facing execution for treason and espionage. The character development has blossomed. And the details and writing remain unapproachable. The author has a magical touch with all the historical details bringing this one to life on the pages.<br /> <br />Yes, this reader cried. And sat on the edge of my chair most of the time. The love between these two is challenged at every turn. The sadness is almost unbearable. How much more must they endure?<br /><br />I'm about to find out as I proceed to the next book with a hopeful heart. One full review covering all three books will be posted upon completion of the final book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1022702056107299927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xJbLt8C2GHpvD0kRcT33HH5v6lflqkSIENGvEDksHk7+sKJle+jREsgk/XCGyP3DqDANnysnyu9Lr+mh9G/s1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cHEg/2Y/7TtQjmvIWVtEspdio0ZbCfTWMHSWDeaB2sxKV0kt3WEkU/el36murk5tQT1EjpWEerFrCtC8K8IoVg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/47499.Paullina_Simons">About Paullina Simons</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/47499.Paullina_Simons"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1263597025p3/47499.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/47499.Paullina_Simons">Paullina Simons
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,168
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14388742327423061362">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br/><br/>After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullin</span>
  <span id="freeText14388742327423061362" style="display:none">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br /><br />After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullina wrote her first novel <i>Tully</i>. Through word of mouth that book was welcomed by readers all over the world. <br /><br />She continued with more novels, including <i>Red Leaves, Eleven Hours, The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i> (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>), <i>The Summer Garden</i> and <i>The Girl in Times Square</i> (also known as <i>Lily</i>). Many of Paullina's novels have reached international bestseller lists. <br /><br />Apart from her novels, Paullina has also written a cookbook, <i>Tatiana's Table</i>, which is a collection of recipes, short stories and recollections from her best selling trilogy of novels, <i>The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i>, (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>) and <i>The Summer Garden</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14388742327423061362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
